\Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a99b029b978e54f5fe34e42122193ec6a}\index{CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}!biGaussianPdf@{biGaussianPdf}}
\index{biGaussianPdf@{biGaussianPdf}!CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{biGaussianPdf()}{biGaussianPdf()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a99b029b978e54f5fe34e42122193ec6a} 
\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}} CAP::\+\+MATH::\+bi\+Gaussian\+Pdf (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{y}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{sigmax}{ = {\ttfamily 1}, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{sigmay}{ = {\ttfamily 1}, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{rho}{ = {\ttfamily 0}, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x0}{ = {\ttfamily 0}, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{y0}{ = {\ttfamily 0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

Probability density function of the bi-\/dimensional (Gaussian) distribution.

\[ p(x) = {1 \over 2 \pi \sigma_x \sigma_y \sqrt{1-\rho^2}} \exp (-((x-x0)^2/\sigma_x^2 + (y-y0)^2/\sigma_y^2 - 2 \rho x y/(\sigma_x\sigma_y))/2(1-\rho^2)) \]

For detailed description see \href{http://mathworld.wolfram.com/BivariateNormalDistribution.html}{\texttt{Mathworld}}. It can also be evaluated using \+\#normal\+\_\+pdf which will call the same implementation.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em x} & x variable \\
\hline
{\em y} & y variable \\
\hline
{\em sigmax} & the stdev in x \\
\hline
{\em sigmay} & the stdev in y \\
\hline
{\em rho} & correlation, must be between -\/1,1 \\
\hline
{\em x0} & the offset in x \\
\hline
{\em y0} & the offset in y \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

template$<$typename Iterator, typename Element$>$ \\
Iterator CAP::\+\+MATH::\+binary\+Search (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Iterator}]{first}{, }\item[{Iterator}]{last}{, }\item[{Element}]{value}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Binary search in an array defined by its iterators.

The values in the iterators range are supposed to be sorted prior to this call. If match is found, function returns position of element. If no match found, function gives nearest element smaller than value. \Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a699946412fe0bda5272c2e4d4d3f8875}\index{CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}!binarySearch@{binarySearch}}

Bubble sort variant to obtain the order of an array\textquotesingle{}s elements into an index in order to do more useful things than the standard built in functions. 
\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\doxymbox{\texttt{in}}  & {\em Narr} & number of array elements \\
\hline
\doxymbox{\texttt{in}}  & {\em \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}values\+Array} & is unchanged; \\
\hline
\doxymbox{\texttt{in}}  & {\em \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}order\+Array} & is the array of indices corresponding to the descending value of values\+Array with order\+Array\+[0]\+ corresponding to the largest values\+Array value and order\+Array\+[Narr]\+ the smallest.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a874689084b382bc5f6419ef9504dd91c} 
\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}} CAP::\+\+MATH::\+f\+Distribution\+Pdf (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{n}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{m}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x0}{ = {\ttfamily 0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

Probability density function of the F-\/distribution.

\[ p_{n,m}(x) = \frac{\Gamma(\frac{n+m}{2})}{\Gamma(\frac{n}{2}) \Gamma(\frac{m}{2})} n^{n/2} m^{m/2} x^{n/2 -1} (m+nx)^{-(n+m)/2} \]

for x\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}=0. For detailed description see \href{http://mathworld.wolfram.com/F-Distribution.html}{\texttt{Mathworld}}. \Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_aec69de2ad4f665e70d731acd8fc98942}\index{CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}!for@{for}}

\[ p(x) = {1 \over \Gamma(\alpha) \theta^{\alpha}} x^{\alpha-1} e^{-x/\theta} \]

Probability density function of the normal (Gaussian) distribution.

\[ p(x) = {1 \over \sqrt{2 \pi \sigma^2}} e^{-x^2 / 2\sigma^2} \]

\Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_ac5bb1d3cbb6bcee73a16381c081704d9}\index{CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}!landauCdf@{landauCdf}}
\index{landauCdf@{landauCdf}!CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{landauCdf()}{landauCdf()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_ac5bb1d3cbb6bcee73a16381c081704d9} 
\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}} CAP::\+\+MATH::\+landau\+Cdf (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{xi}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x0}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a0156b4369093dadbc204a9be78d5e8cd}\index{CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}!landauPdf@{landauPdf}}
\index{landauPdf@{landauPdf}!CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{landauPdf()}{landauPdf()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a0156b4369093dadbc204a9be78d5e8cd} 
\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}} CAP::\+\+MATH::\+landau\+Pdf (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{xi}{ = {\ttfamily 1}, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x0}{ = {\ttfamily 0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Probability density function of the Landau distribution:\+ \[ p(x) = \frac{1}{\xi} \phi (\lambda) \] with \[  \phi(\lambda) = \frac{1}{2 \pi i}\int_{c-i\infty}^{c+i\infty} e^{\lambda s + s \log{s}} ds\] where $\lambda = (x-_x0)/\xi$. For a detailed description see K.\+S. K\"{o}lbig and B. Schorr, \doxylink{class_a}{A} program package for the Landau distribution, \href{http://dx.doi.org/10.1016/0010-4655(84)90085-7}{\texttt{Computer Phys. Comm. 31 (1984) 97-\/111}} \href{http://dx.doi.org/10.1016/j.cpc.2008.03.002}{\texttt{\+[Erratum-\/ibid. 178 (2008) 972]\+}}. The same algorithms as in \href{https://cern-tex.web.cern.ch/cern-tex/shortwrupsdir/g110/top.html}{\texttt{CERNLIB}} (DENLAN) is used


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em x} & The argument $x$ \\
\hline
{\em xi} & The width parameter $\xi$ \\
\hline
{\em x0} & The location parameter $_x0$ \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{locateMinimum()}{locateMinimum()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a38c2a66130215398f044c36d946e723e} 
template$<$typename Iterator$>$ \\
Iterator CAP::\+\+MATH::\+locate\+Minimum (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Iterator}]{first}{, }\item[{Iterator}]{last}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Returns index of array with the minimum element. If more than one element is minimum returns first found.

Implement here since this one is found to be faster (mainly on 64 bit machines) than stl generic implementation. When performing the comparison, the STL implementation needs to de-\/reference both the array iterator and the iterator pointing to the resulting minimum location

Returns index of array with the minimum element. If more than one element is minimum returns first found. \Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_ae550c6152daa4a9ccca6bc3760c6ff45}\index{CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}!locateMinimum@{locateMinimum}}

\Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a1d40afb2e80c8b84856c28768054e108}\index{CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}!logNormalPdf@{logNormalPdf}}
\index{logNormalPdf@{logNormalPdf}!CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{logNormalPdf()}{logNormalPdf()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a1d40afb2e80c8b84856c28768054e108} 
\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}} CAP::\+\+MATH::\+log\+Normal\+Pdf (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{m}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{s}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x0}{ = {\ttfamily 0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

Probability density function of the lognormal distribution.

\[ p(x) = {1 \over x \sqrt{2 \pi s^2} } e^{-(\ln{x} - m)^2/2 s^2} \]

for x\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}0. For detailed description see \href{http://mathworld.wolfram.com/LogNormalDistribution.html}{\texttt{Mathworld}}. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em x} & x variable \\
\hline
{\em m} & M = 0 for lognormal \\
\hline
{\em \doxylink{namespace_c_a_p_acc63048b8c9b011cfbea59b40e02e8f8}{s}} & scale parameter (not the sigma of the distribution which is not even defined) \\
\hline
{\em x0} & location parameter, corresponds approximately to the most probable value. For x0 = 0, sigma = 1, the \+\_\+xmpv = -\/0.\+22278 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rms()}{rms()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a84f7d257f1720384a38253727f37b91f} 
template$<$typename T, typename Iterator$>$ \\
T CAP::\+\+MATH::\+rms (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Iterator}]{first}{, }\item[{Iterator}]{last}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Returns the root mean square (rms) of the data identified by the given iterators. Use the two pass algorithm, which is slower (! a factor of 2) but much more precise. Since we have a vector the 2 pass algorithm is still faster than the Welford algorithm. \Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a76f60ed598f9060112893ce41a09bedf}\index{CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}!scalarProduct@{scalarProduct}}

\Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_ac651b8c22a9a0fbc11e15d3637d39f84}\index{CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}!tDistributionPdf@{tDistributionPdf}}
\index{tDistributionPdf@{tDistributionPdf}!CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{tDistributionPdf()}{tDistributionPdf()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_ac651b8c22a9a0fbc11e15d3637d39f84} 
\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}} CAP::\+\+MATH::\+t\+Distribution\+Pdf (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{r}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x0}{ = {\ttfamily 0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

Probability density function of Student\textquotesingle{}s t-\/distribution.

\[ p_{r}(x) = \frac{\Gamma(\frac{r+1}{2})}{\sqrt{r \pi}\Gamma(\frac{r}{2})} \left( 1+\frac{x^2}{r}\right)^{-(r+1)/2}  \]

for $k \geq 0$. For detailed description see \href{http://mathworld.wolfram.com/Studentst-Distribution.html}{\texttt{Mathworld}}. \Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_1_1_m_a_t_h_a38322c471d71361f83acb4585045a019}\index{CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}!totalEntries@{totalEntries}}
\index{totalEntries@{totalEntries}!CAP::MATH@{CAP::MATH}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{totalEntries()}{totalEntries()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/4]}}

Probability density function of the uniform (flat) distribution.

\[ p(x) = {1 \over (b-a)} \]
